  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_813d0eb4-84ec-4223-9519-3837995fb954'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/82689674-anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2412763613" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11391205430252259662">After finishing this book, I realized that the desire to write a review came not so much out of courtesy to each author of the books I read, but to allow these erupting emotions of mine a chance to spill out so that I can be free of the turbulence that shook my soul after arriving at this book's conclusion. And so, before I offer my thoughts over the book as a whole, I need to vent! <br/><br/>I am shocked! Thoroughly shocked!! I am appalled too, angry and sad!<br/><br/>What the main character did at the end made me</span>
  <span id="freeText11391205430252259662" style="display:none">After finishing this book, I realized that the desire to write a review came not so much out of courtesy to each author of the books I read, but to allow these erupting emotions of mine a chance to spill out so that I can be free of the turbulence that shook my soul after arriving at this book's conclusion. And so, before I offer my thoughts over the book as a whole, I need to vent! <br /><br />I am shocked! Thoroughly shocked!! I am appalled too, angry and sad!<br /><br />What the main character did at the end made me wonder if having him as the new ruler of the Sun Elves was not actually a good thing as I had initially expected when the book began! I honestly have no words! All I can say is that I hate Asharal! I hate him! I really do. Very few characters in fictional books have made me feel so malicious towards them, as Asharal has now made me feel! I genuinely hate him and do not know how I can express this feeling in more detail! <br /><br />But with that said, now that I can breathe, my thoughts over the entirety of the book are positive. The plot blew me away. The twist at the end (despite how much it shook my entire being when realizing what had actually happened) was incredibly well written, a very smart way of constructing a story, and despite how much I loathe the main character, I cannot deny his appeal nor what a strong character he made throughout the book. <br /><br />Asharal is incredibly vivid and made this book great!<br /><br />After reading The Evening Tide, I am eager to read more, to submerge myself in this new world of elves and plot twists, and to once more experience such explosive emotions</span>
  <a data-text-id="11391205430252259662" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2591706262" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2591706262" />
    <a title="Joc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68172472-joc"><img alt="Joc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537103104p2/68172472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2591706262?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joc" href="/user/show/68172472-joc">Joc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68172472-joc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2591706262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8570089418838785470">The island of the Sun Elves is ruled by the Wind Family but not everyone is in favour of them. The secret to immortality has been discovered but there is no certainty that the ruler, Father of the Sun, will share the gift with his people. Asharal is certain he won’t and is in the process of preparing to overthrow the Winds.<br/><br/>There are a number of things that made this a really interesting and engaging read. The story is told in the first person from various points of view but not from Asharal’s wh</span>
  <span id="freeText8570089418838785470" style="display:none">The island of the Sun Elves is ruled by the Wind Family but not everyone is in favour of them. The secret to immortality has been discovered but there is no certainty that the ruler, Father of the Sun, will share the gift with his people. Asharal is certain he won’t and is in the process of preparing to overthrow the Winds.<br /><br />There are a number of things that made this a really interesting and engaging read. The story is told in the first person from various points of view but not from Asharal’s which was wonderfully odd because the story centres around him. Asharal is infatuated with Dawn, a young elvess born of ordinary village people, and it is partly her point of view that we see things from.<br /><br />Another thing that struck me was that I wasn’t sure whose side I was on for most of the story and that rarely happens to me. Dawn’s parents were in opposition on their allegiance to the rulers, Dawn’s allegiance was with Asharal, the Son of the Father didn’t seem like a bad person and because Asharal’s point of view is the one we don’t get, it was hard to gauge where he was coming from. He clearly wanted a better life for the Sun Elves but I wasn’t sure that the violence was justifiable. <br /><br />For most of this read, it was an easy four star rating. It’s well-written, different from my expectations and I really wanted to see where the story went because I knew there was something elusive happening. And then I got close to the end and everything fell into place. It’s fantastically clever and just to cement my realisation, I flipped through it again.<br /><br /><i>Book received from the author for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="8570089418838785470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420599736" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1237294500168920331">It took a while before everything clicked, but once I figured out the order of things, this book really impressed me. It surprised me too. I didn't have high expectations when beginning the book; I only started reading it because everyone was recommending it, and I am glad they did. <br/><br/>Elves, battle, plot twist, overthrows, and magic! My cup of tea!!</span>

<div id="review_2696761966" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696761966" />
    <a title="Mak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66553282-mak"><img alt="Mak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546523711p2/66553282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2696761966?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mak" href="/user/show/66553282-mak">Mak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66553282-mak?shelf=smss">smss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696761966" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14806645396128874595"><b>I have edited my review and have simply added a short summary of the book (So, the whole review is full of spoilers). I came across a few reviews were people were left confused and because of lack of understanding they rather reviewed it harshly. It is a shame not to give the author the credit he deserves or at least the chance to understand his writing. This author certainly does not follow the usual and conservative way of writing and does not hand you out the answers right there ready for the</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14806645396128874595" style="display:none"><b>I have edited my review and have simply added a short summary of the book (So, the whole review is full of spoilers). I came across a few reviews were people were left confused and because of lack of understanding they rather reviewed it harshly. It is a shame not to give the author the credit he deserves or at least the chance to understand his writing. This author certainly does not follow the usual and conservative way of writing and does not hand you out the answers right there ready for the taking, but he rather follows a more unorthodox and unique writing where the reader gets to invest more in it and it feels like a mind puzzle which once solved leaves you content. Obviously, there are questions and things that might be disorienting, but this is a totally new fantasy realm, built from scratch and which introduces various times, events and characters with strong political and religious backgrounds and stories. It has twists and turns, it gets light and dark (maybe slightly more on the darker side with each new book) and there is nothing simple or ordinary about it. One should read at least the first 3 books in order to get a bigger and clearer picture of this world. All I am saying, it is worth it! So, enjoy :)))) </b><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The story begins with an Elvess who lives with her father and mother. They are Sun Elves who are ruled by the Winds and from the Sunchair rules the Father of the Sun who has promised to make all Sun Elves Immortal by giving them water from the Pool of Eternity. The story is built around prophecies and is about the drive of revenge, power and love. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />We are also introduced to a powerful and arrogant Highborn Sun Elf, Asharal Evening. The Elvess, who is called either Pebble or Rose by her parents, is actually meeting in secret (from everyone but her parents) with Asharal, who calls her Dawn. Dawn/Pebble/Rose is actually in love with Asharal and she is presented as a very timid, simple and naïve Elvess. <br /><br />Asharal on the other hand, even though there are moments in which he appears gentle and genuine with her and is rather cultivated, is very judgmental, arrogant, secretive and even rude. (later we get to see how he is also ruthless). He feels that most are beneath him and is driven by hatred, and who with the help of his brother Sharal plan to take the Sunchair and become Immortals. <br /><br />Part of the story is told by Dawn, who becomes reckless and endangers herself in order to be with Asharal. There’s a scene where she nearly gets raped and Asharal saves her, showing that he has feelings for her as well, but apparently due to his painful past and his future plans can’t appreciate or even see what he has found in her. <br /><br />The rest of the story (except for the epilogue) is told by the Son of the Father. He, in contrast to Asharal, is very kind and thoughtful. He does not agree with how his Father rules and in general we see a very likable and decent Elf. During his first narration of the story, he talks of his Lady Elwyn and how Asharal and his brother have killed his Father, the Sunchair has been betrayed and finally the two brothers kill both Lady Elwyn and then the Son of the Father. Asharal, right before killing Elwyn, has a moment of recognition and regret in his eyes and that’s the moment when the reader begins to question the characters and the story. <br /><br />The narration is one on one. One part told by Dawn and the next by the Son and on and on. It is during the second narration of the Son that the reader (should) realizes that his side of the story is going backwards and that the narration of Dawn is going forward and both narrations come to meet right before the present (so nothing up to that part in the book is in the now), where finally everything clicks back in place: That Dawn is actually Lady ELwyn, who even though was in love with Asharal and was supporting his beliefs against the Winds and was firmly told by him to stay away from them, circumstances become as such that the Son of the Father invites her to his quarters. She is in a very difficult situation and cannot deny his offer and so she follows him. <br /><br />Asharal on the other hand was planning to invade the Wind Tower and dethrone the Winds and during all this time, he has been executing his plans. However, after killing the Father, when he goes after the Son and finds Elwyn with him instead of giving her the chance to explain and hear her out, he just calls her a betrayer and kills her without mercy. <br /><br />Asharal also drinks the water of the Eternity pool, becomes a Highborn Immortal and with him begins a new reign, a new era for the Sun Elves. <br /><br />In the epilogue we also see Elwyn’s parents coming to claim their daughter’s body and when her mother tells him that she loved him and that that was her only crime, instead of admitting his mistake, he orders them killed. <br /><br />In the book, we get a glimpse of the Blues Elves, meaning that there are more Elves out there and also we learn of the prophecy of Sharal’s death by the hand of a Moon (Moon Elves), anticipating what the next installments in the series will reveal. <br />So, this pretty much sums the story and makes a hell of an introduction with a big loud boom into a very fascinating and unique world. <br /><br /><br />Third time reading this book, a brilliant start to an amazing series and every time is a delight!<br /><br /><u>Original review:</u><br /><br />Damn you for fooling me!<br /><br />Never have I ever read a book and re-read it immediately upon finishing reading it. <br />The author is simply brilliant and had me fooled. One should read this book in one sitting, otherwise you risk getting lost within the pages. I was too arrogant and a big a fool to have judged this book badly in my mind, as I was reading and not realizing at first the brilliancy of how the author kept switching form past to present. Who could have thought that the end is at the beginning? <br /><br />I thought it was annoying that I had read nearly the whole book without being able to recall if the main female character has an actual name. I had some suspicions, but it was done in such a way that I wasn't sure. And, then, at 83% of the book the name is spoken loud and clear and everything clicks back in order and understanding settles in. I could tell that many scenes were interacting with the past, but I couldn’t really figure out what was happening. What a unique way of writing!<br /><br />I was so frustrated by the main characters Elwyn and Asharal, the former for her ignorance, naïveté and childishness and the latter for his arrogance, ruthlessness and conflicting personality, that I couldn’t see beyond the tree and finally look at the forest. <br /><br />What can I say about the major plot twist and the oh so brilliant way of putting the facts together? The author used past and future in a magnificent way where the past was moving forward and the future back and forth creating a sort of butterfly effect in the reader’s mind. <br /><br />Asharal is a very strong character and through the book the reader cannot decide whether this is a likeable character or someone to hate. Personally, I thought he was an ass! I could on the one hand understand his thirst for vengeance, but the cruelty in which he excelled without offering the benefit of the doubt and without being just, had me wanting to rip him off from the pages of the book. On the other hand, he showed kindness and tenderness and a brutal sense of protection which caused me to shiver, and I couldn’t understand why he looked down on Dawn and what his intentions originally were with her. <br /><br /><i>You are right. Asharal is one of a kind. But that doesn’t mean he is the only one of a kind.</i><br /><br />The Son of the Father was one to steal another’s heart. He was kind and passionate and the Suns would have flourished if he were to become Father of the Sun. I really liked him and I thoroughly enjoyed his narrative more. <br /><br /><i>I encouraged her to have a taste, and she bit into it, the juice of it spilling out from the corner of her mouth. She wiped at her lips hurriedly, tried to compensate for the untidiness of the bite, without realizing that I thoroughly enjoyed watching how it all took place.</i><br /><br />This is overall the perfect start to an amazing series, and the author's creativity and originality catch the reader's attention and you are sucked into the story. But, I think what makes this book special is the style of writing, the forth and back in events done in such a unique way that most are fooled and only realize it toward the end. It is simply brilliant. As for the characters, Asharal is the one that stands out -some come to hate him and others to admire him- and he is one of those characters that one cannot easily forget. There's a great world behind these stories, a world of fantasy, legends and prophecies that is worth getting to now and explore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14806645396128874595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/87400615-edward">Edward</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2553290757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3140812189613655460">Clever!!<br/><br/>I have never read a book told in this way before. Admittedly I was very confused throughout but luckily, the main character Asharal kept me wanting to know more and it eventually became clear that despite my confusion, something was up and when at last everything connected and I understood what that was, I was flabbergasted. <br/><br/>The structure of the story aside; these elves are an impoverished race, live in an era that seems to be the dark ages? I don't know? But they are very interesting. <br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText3140812189613655460" style="display:none">Clever!!<br /><br />I have never read a book told in this way before. Admittedly I was very confused throughout but luckily, the main character Asharal kept me wanting to know more and it eventually became clear that despite my confusion, something was up and when at last everything connected and I understood what that was, I was flabbergasted. <br /><br />The structure of the story aside; these elves are an impoverished race, live in an era that seems to be the dark ages? I don't know? But they are very interesting. <br /><br />The main character (as I have suggested above) is very gripping, is definitely the driving force of this short story, despite the fact that we never actually see the story unfold through his eyes, but rather, through the eyes of an elvess who is obsessed with him and an enemy who is afraid of him, hates him. <br /><br />The only drawback for me really was that the elvess who loves Asharal is irritating but forgivable due to the impression she gives of being too sheltered and therefore, naive. I really appreciated how her character seemed to develop from this naive and annoying elvess to one who was slowly broadening her thinking (thanks to Asharal). That redeemed her in my eyes. <br /><br />What made this book great for me was its narrative and how well thought out was its plot!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3140812189613655460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13684462072871087902">Without giving too much away I must say this was definitely a different approach to story telling. I am intrigued by the universe that Forsyth has built as well as the characters who occupy it. As I read this the phrase, "Dance with the devil you know" came to mind, especially when I got to the conclusion. The old saying that power corrupts has a corollary - power tends to attract those who are easily corruptible. As I reach the conclusion of "Tide" and anticipate the next installment, I wonder </span>
  <span id="freeText13684462072871087902" style="display:none">Without giving too much away I must say this was definitely a different approach to story telling. I am intrigued by the universe that Forsyth has built as well as the characters who occupy it. As I read this the phrase, "Dance with the devil you know" came to mind, especially when I got to the conclusion. The old saying that power corrupts has a corollary - power tends to attract those who are easily corruptible. As I reach the conclusion of "Tide" and anticipate the next installment, I wonder if Asharal is really savior - or if the Evening will be worse than the Wind. I look forward to the next book...</span>

    <a title="Nikita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82926209-nikita"><img alt="Nikita" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419223198?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikita" href="/user/show/82926209-nikita">Nikita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419223198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14481327835051012281">The Evening Tide is an intricate and exciting story that took my breath away. The way the author combined two timelines, engaged the reader and sucked me into the character's lives made it difficult to put the book down. The story twists and turns in a way that shows the author's insane creativity. He brings characters to life by giving words to feelings that many have felt for years. I loved this book, and I am excited to see the rest of the work that that Jeremy comes up with!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120498939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2751447046135660211">A super intriguing read that sucks you into a fantastic world where you can't help but feel that all is not what it seems. The character development is amazing; each one evokes a strong, intuitive response. More than just a well thought out story, the author is not shy to challenge the reader to think beyond what they expect. The complexity of the plot lines taunt the reader to engage on a deeper level where the reward is compelling and engaging! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2585079743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2585079743" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2154195-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370984520p2/2154195.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2585079743?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/2154195-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2154195-diane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2585079743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4645218518965082344">This is a fresh take on the fantasy genre and would be a good one for lovers of elfin worlds or puzzle-solvers. The structure of the story is creative, and the author made an effort to do something unexpected and thought-provoking. <br/><br/>Random thoughts provoked in me:<br/><br/>I hate clingy, desperate women. Rose/Pebble/Dawn, etc. needs to get a grip. Asharal sure seems like an asshole to me. And yep, seems I’m right. <br/><br/>I’m confused about a number of things. I actually went back to try to figure out a few of the</span>
  <span id="freeText4645218518965082344" style="display:none">This is a fresh take on the fantasy genre and would be a good one for lovers of elfin worlds or puzzle-solvers. The structure of the story is creative, and the author made an effort to do something unexpected and thought-provoking. <br /><br />Random thoughts provoked in me:<br /><br />I hate clingy, desperate women. Rose/Pebble/Dawn, etc. needs to get a grip. Asharal sure seems like an asshole to me. And yep, seems I’m right. <br /><br />I’m confused about a number of things. I actually went back to try to figure out a few of them once I understood the structure. First, I struggled to understand who the narrator was of each chapter. When I went back, I still couldn’t figure out a few of them. Next, Elwyn and Alwyn sound an awful lot alike and both are described as “traitors.” I’m struggling to get some of these characters straight, and the above put me into a quandary, but it doesn’t help that the main character is called so many different things. Trying hard not to give anything away here, but I’m not sure whether Asharal is right about . . . let’s call her Elwyn. . . or not. Seems like kind of, maybe, but that seems like a big 180 to me. The Son of the Father -- good guy? Bad guy? I’m not sure. Why did he beckon Elwyn? And is Wind bad and Sun good? I need more information to make that determination with confidence. As should be obvious, I’m left with some lingering questions, some of which may reflect my own lack of mental acuity. I don’t mind if I’m left with some questions, particularly when a sequel may provide answers, but more breadcrumbs and glimpses inside these characters’ heads please!<br /><br />So the bottom line is that there’s something interesting here, but maybe you need to be smarter than me to fully grasp it. I would read the sequel though in the hopes of getting some answers. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4645218518965082344" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2248036789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer989794643059888391">Once I figured out how the author wrote this book(going both forward and backward simultaneously in the storyline), I realized how genius the story was as a whole. You almost think you only have half of the story until the final line of the final chapter; and then suddenly everything connects. This new world is very believable and the characters are quite relatable.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6845961-shannon-hutcheson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2877024116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15926958200215244077">While I enjoyed how the author wrote, his prose was so eloquent and definitely eluded an earlier more medieval time, the storyline wasn't as "mind blowing" as some of the previous reviews suggested. In fact, I found the ending kind of inevitable. There was no sudden revelation for me at all. What struck me was that other reviewers thought the ending WAS surprising. <br/><br/>Anyhow, the storyline is fairly unique. I'd like to see more magic than there is, and how unique and different that magic might be t</span>
  <span id="freeText15926958200215244077" style="display:none">While I enjoyed how the author wrote, his prose was so eloquent and definitely eluded an earlier more medieval time, the storyline wasn't as "mind blowing" as some of the previous reviews suggested. In fact, I found the ending kind of inevitable. There was no sudden revelation for me at all. What struck me was that other reviewers thought the ending WAS surprising. <br /><br />Anyhow, the storyline is fairly unique. I'd like to see more magic than there is, and how unique and different that magic might be to other typical fantasy books. I also look forward to learning how and why the weaponry our main man had and how it came to exist. Hopefully, there will be more about that. If not, I'll be disappointed as the book was pretty short already. There doesn't seem to be a whole lot of actual detail other than about the character's goal and how the 1st person view of the storytelling character saw him. But overall the main characters are interesting and believable. Enough to get me started on the second book. I hope it is longer, I read this one in one sitting in a matter of hours. Not that that is necessarily a bad thing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15926958200215244077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2534767897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16164080145917908476"><strong>Love this one</strong><br/><br/>When I began this book I was drawn in by the purity and simplicity of the elvess who had a pure yet obsessive love for an aloof elf. He exuded power, Grace and superiority. I found I didn't quite know what to think of him. He kept himself separate and guarded. Then the next chapter you would get a glimpse of the royal sun elves. There are rumors and violence in their world. Back and forth between scenes until the epilogue where the two worlds collide and you're left with your jaw on</span>
  <span id="freeText16164080145917908476" style="display:none"><strong>Love this one</strong><br /><br />When I began this book I was drawn in by the purity and simplicity of the elvess who had a pure yet obsessive love for an aloof elf. He exuded power, Grace and superiority. I found I didn't quite know what to think of him. He kept himself separate and guarded. Then the next chapter you would get a glimpse of the royal sun elves. There are rumors and violence in their world. Back and forth between scenes until the epilogue where the two worlds collide and you're left with your jaw on the floor. I want more from this world. It's a clever writing style and intriguing characters that keep you reading late into the night.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16164080145917908476" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SZmVDFxJclvJOfn9z4SfnYHD0XMTJaidH03wRiTcyqmSJ7cK4gwuPNzwuUo5fXGuQlDAMQtHSjJn8g71mTYZFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Mo8DjxBDi8UVQyk19Y3Yft7+nk5B2yHuPnEbpgupU+XpMSGJrgbXogCKaYIDdDZNHW2PDFm5w0FGzuUVtkOAWw==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
